## Section 001: Plugin Command Development Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not yet define when a plugin slash command is the correct extension surface, how its instruction contract should be bounded, or which installation, permission, interaction, recovery, and distribution evidence must accompany it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a command turns user intent into model instructions at invocation time, so clarity and permission scope shape behavior while portable paths and layered tests determine whether the same workflow survives installation and edge cases
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the capability must run automatically on events, maintain specialized autonomous reasoning, expose an external service protocol, persist configuration independently, or execute high-risk operations without an explicit human gate
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for Claude Code plugin slash-command design and validation, not as current authoritative documentation for every extension surface or product release
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a surface-selection matrix, instruction contract, least-privilege and portability rules, interaction boundaries, layered verification, recovery expectations, distribution gates, and explicit freshness caveats
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a command is an interface contract around model behavior, not merely a saved prompt; distribution turns every implicit local assumption into a potential installation or safety defect
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to choose a focused command for an explicitly invoked, repeatable agent workflow; write directives to Claude, keep frontmatter minimal, grant least-required tools, use plugin-root paths, validate inputs, expose recovery, and test discovery through real invocation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a command turns user intent into model instructions at invocation time, so clarity and permission scope shape behavior while portable paths and layered tests determine whether the same workflow survives installation and edge cases
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the capability must run automatically on events, maintain specialized autonomous reasoning, expose an external service protocol, persist configuration independently, or execute high-risk operations without an explicit human gate
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for Claude Code plugin slash-command design and validation, not as current authoritative documentation for every extension surface or product release
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a surface-selection matrix, instruction contract, least-privilege and portability rules, interaction boundaries, layered verification, recovery expectations, distribution gates, and explicit freshness caveats
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a command is an interface contract around model behavior, not merely a saved prompt; distribution turns every implicit local assumption into a potential installation or safety defect

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the capability must run automatically on events, maintain specialized autonomous reasoning, expose an external service protocol, persist configuration independently, or execute high-risk operations without an explicit human gate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are writing marketing copy instead of instructions, granting broad Bash access, hardcoding installation paths, confusing arguments with interactive choices, embedding complex program logic in Markdown, assuming discovery, and omitting cancel or cleanup behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the workflow has a clear manual trigger, bounded goal, inspectable inputs, predictable tool needs, useful user-facing help, and a result that can be verified without hidden automatic execution

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Command Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: use a hook for event-driven enforcement, a skill for reusable knowledge, an agent for delegated autonomy, MCP for external tools or resources, settings for persistent policy, or a tested script behind a thin command when deterministic logic dominates

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sixteen local command-development paths as separate rows even though they form eight byte-identical archive and live-path pairs, then adds three MCP links whose subject is adjacent integration rather than slash-command semantics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because counting duplicate bytes as independent support inflates apparent evidence, while allowing MCP resources to prove command behavior confuses two extension contracts with different invocation and lifecycle semantics
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: sixteen rows are presented as sixteen independent confirmations, a marketplace example becomes current product truth, MCP documentation defines slash-command frontmatter, or an inference has no claim-level provenance
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this provenance model to the frozen nineteen rows and distinguish source evidence from later installed-product tests
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add duplicate-lineage handling, claim-specific authority, external adjacency limits, current-version verification rules, and a provenance ledger while retaining every original path and URL
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that duplicate detection changes both context and epistemics: it halves redundant reading while preventing copied files from masquerading as independent consensus

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says to load local sources, check public analogues, and add verification, but it does not state that a command is an instruction interface whose quality depends on surface fit, least privilege, portability, observable branches, and installed-product behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Markdown wording drives model behavior, frontmatter shapes invocation context, and plugin packaging changes paths and discovery; therefore prose, permissions, resources, and lifecycle tests jointly define the interface
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: automatic enforcement, deep delegated autonomy, external protocol integration, hidden persistent state, or irreversible execution is forced into a prompt file merely because commands are easy to add
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the thesis for plugin command decisions and treat adjacent extension docs or current product tests as separate evidence classes
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the generic synthesis with a surface-fit rule, four-layer command contract, failure alternatives, installed-path verification, and an explicit archived-versus-current evidence boundary
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the command file is simultaneously prompt, permission declaration, package entry point, and user-facing API; a defect in any one layer can invalidate otherwise excellent instructions
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to select the command surface only for explicit reusable invocation, express one outcome as directives to Claude, expose a small argument or question contract, constrain tools, move deterministic complexity into plugin resources, and validate the installed user journey

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed includes one generated-reference verifier, while command correctness also requires structured metadata parsing, plugin discovery, substitution, permission, interaction, resource, workflow, failure, and distribution evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because static artifact integrity cannot prove product discovery or model behavior, and a successful happy-path invocation cannot prove least privilege, failure containment, or cross-install path correctness
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: grep counts frontmatter delimiters as full YAML validation, help discovery is assumed from file existence, scripts are trusted without exit checks, manual success replaces regression fixtures, or reference validation certifies a command
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: separate QA for this reference from QA for command artifacts and from tests of external systems those commands may call
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a layered gate matrix, structured parsing requirement, installed-plugin fixture, security and recovery cases, evidence packet, and current focused validator while retaining the seed command

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed frames adopt, adapt, and avoid around source agreement but omits the actual tradeoffs among a simple prompt, arguments, interactive questions, script delegation, workflow state, and alternate extension surfaces
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every added question, tool, script, state file, and integration increases capability and user value but also expands ambiguity, permission, recovery, compatibility, and maintenance surfaces
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: local and external agreement is treated as enough, adaptation papers over invalid syntax, avoidance has no alternate route, or marketplace ambition justifies premature complexity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: make the choice per workflow and risk class rather than adopting a single command architecture across an entire plugin
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reframe the four seed options around interface complexity, lifecycle cost, permission risk, portability, partial orchestration, and alternate surfaces
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the cheapest reliable design often keeps the command declarative and moves repeatable mechanics into a separately testable component
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to adopt simple explicit workflows, adapt when permissions or packaging require narrower mechanics, avoid when trigger or lifecycle mismatches, and treat stateful or mutating commands as higher-cost designs with stronger tests
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because every added question, tool, script, state file, and integration increases capability and user value but also expands ambiguity, permission, recovery, compatibility, and maintenance surfaces
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; local and external agreement is treated as enough, adaptation papers over invalid syntax, avoidance has no alternate route, or marketplace ambition justifies premature complexity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: make the choice per workflow and risk class rather than adopting a single command architecture across an entire plugin
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: reframe the four seed options around interface complexity, lifecycle cost, permission risk, portability, partial orchestration, and alternate surfaces

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks role, options, hierarchy, artifact, examples, metrics, and routing, but omits command surface fit, directive quality, metadata parsing, permissions, resource portability, side effects, state, recovery, installed invocation, and removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a missing layer can leave a command structurally valid yet undiscoverable, overprivileged, nonportable, state-corrupting, or impossible for an unfamiliar user to recover
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: checkmarks have no evidence, parsing substitutes for invocation, happy paths substitute for denial and interruption, documentation claims exceed tested platforms, or marketplace readiness is inferred from polish
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the full checklist to published plugin commands and document justified reductions for local read-only use
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend each seed category with evidence pointers, command-contract gates, risk-based applicability, package lifecycle checks, and a final reviewer replay
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that completeness is scope-relative but never implicit; reducing distribution or effects can reduce required gates, whereas merely calling a command simple cannot

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing follows keywords, several extension references are opened at once, a command remains responsible for another component's lifecycle, or handoff results silently broaden permissions or scope

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed sets one task, ten source files, three delegated subtasks, and a completion audit, but command complexity is more directly driven by inputs, tool capabilities, side effects, workflow states, integrations, and distribution environments
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because natural-language orchestration becomes harder to reason about as effects and branches multiply, even when source count remains low; packaging and recovery complexity also grows with audience breadth
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one command performs unrelated setup, migration, deployment, and reporting, parallel delegates mutate shared state, context grows through raw outputs, or a ten-file limit is treated as proof of simplicity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this model for command and review ownership; evaluate external script or server throughput with component-specific methods
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain seed capacity rows but add behavioral dimensions, decomposition triggers, state and integration ownership, context controls, and risk-adjusted evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the binding capacity is reviewable behavior, not prompt length: a short command that calls broad tools can exceed safe workload before a long read-only rubric does
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep one command centered on one user outcome, bound argument and question surfaces, minimize tool classes and integrations, externalize deterministic logic, and split independent state machines or ownership domains
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because natural-language orchestration becomes harder to reason about as effects and branches multiply, even when source count remains low; packaging and recovery complexity also grows with audience breadth
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one command performs unrelated setup, migration, deployment, and reporting, parallel delegates mutate shared state, context grows through raw outputs, or a ten-file limit is treated as proof of simplicity

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the binding capacity is reviewable behavior, not prompt length: a short command that calls broad tools can exceed safe workload before a long read-only rubric does

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: one command performs unrelated setup, migration, deployment, and reporting, parallel delegates mutate shared state, context grows through raw outputs, or a ten-file limit is treated as proof of simplicity

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed sets complete evidence labels, 18-of-20 routing, zero unsupported claims, and universal recovery paths, but it neither marks these as proposed targets nor covers discovery, least privilege, side-effect containment, portability, and cleanup
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because artifact and safety invariants can demand complete compliance, while human-model interaction and diverse installations require empirical cohorts rather than invented certainty
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18 of 20 is advertised as measured accuracy, complete labels imply correct behavior, broad tools pass because the command succeeds, or recovery documentation is counted without an interruption test
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: treat seed values as acceptance proposals or sampling goals, never as achieved product or model reliability
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to classify targets, add lifecycle and least-privilege gates, define empirical cohorts, require denominators and miss handling, and prohibit unsupported achieved-rate claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that command reliability has two axes: interface safety can be gated before release, while behavioral usability must keep learning from real invocations
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers drift, generic guidance, context loss, and tool fanout, but omits command discovery, metadata rejection, substitution errors, permission denial, resource paths, state corruption, partial effects, integration failure, and uninstall residue
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because layer-specific classification avoids unsafe retries and broad rewrites; a help-list failure differs fundamentally from a partial deployment or stale workflow state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all problems become prompt wording, nonzero script exits are summarized away, denied tools trigger broader permissions, partial files are overwritten, or cleanup is attempted without knowing state ownership
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this table for command and plugin-lifecycle failures, while diagnosing called scripts or MCP servers with their component-specific evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the four generic rows and add command-layer taxonomy, side-effect containment, state-aware recovery, reproduction fixtures, and recurrence feedback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that failure handling should trace effect lineage: the correct recovery depends less on the final error message than on which actions occurred before it

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed limits stale-evidence retries and stops on red gates, but it does not define safe command replay, idempotency, state ownership, external side effects, or how arguments and environment must be frozen between attempts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a command retry can repeat shell, filesystem, deployment, or external operations; unchanged prompt repetition may multiply damage while hiding the original failure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the model retries after tool denial by broadening access, network ambiguity triggers duplicate mutation, state is recreated over partial work, a new argument masks the same failure, or concurrency bypasses a lock
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply command-level retry controls and delegate external service or script retry policy to the owning component
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add invocation identity, effect ledger, idempotency and compensation gates, state validation, concurrency ownership, semantic success, and modality-switch exits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure preserves user trust by making uncertainty visible before another invocation converts it into an additional side effect
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retry only after classifying the failed layer, proving previous effects and state, changing a relevant prerequisite, preserving the original input contract, and confirming the next attempt is idempotent or explicitly compensated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a command retry can repeat shell, filesystem, deployment, or external operations; unchanged prompt repetition may multiply damage while hiding the original failure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the model retries after tool denial by broadening access, network ambiguity triggers duplicate mutation, state is recreated over partial work, a new argument masks the same failure, or concurrency bypasses a lock
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply command-level retry controls and delegate external service or script retry policy to the owning component
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add invocation identity, effect ledger, idempotency and compensation gates, state validation, concurrency ownership, semantic success, and modality-switch exits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure preserves user trust by making uncertainty visible before another invocation converts it into an additional side effect

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed tracks loaded sources, proof, timing, tool calls, context, delegation, retries, outcomes, and concise audit evidence but omits command identity, metadata, inputs, permissions, effects, state, resources, installation, and privacy
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because correlating interface, environment, capability, and effect state distinguishes prompt ambiguity from packaging, permission, dependency, or external failures while preserving a reviewable record
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw prompts or command outputs leak data, success-only logs hide containment, tool-call counts have no capability context, filesystem writes are untracked, or installation scope cannot be reconstructed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: capture command lifecycle evidence with least data and route external component telemetry to its owner
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add invocation correlation, version and scope, redacted inputs, metadata and permission state, resource and side-effect events, cancellation, privacy, and reconstruction tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability is useful when it localizes the first contract divergence, not when it merely proves that the model and tools were active
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record command and plugin version, install scope, invocation class, redacted input shape, parsed metadata, granted and denied tools, resource and script status, state transitions, side-effect summary, errors, recovery, and user-visible outcome

- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add invocation correlation, version and scope, redacted inputs, metadata and permission state, resource and side-effect events, cancellation, privacy, and reconstruction tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies observability is useful when it localizes the first contract divergence, not when it merely proves that the model and tools were active

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: raw prompts or command outputs leak data, success-only logs hide containment, tool-call counts have no capability context, filesystem writes are untracked, or installation scope cannot be reconstructed

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires tool and timeout budgets plus a resumable journal for long work, but it does not define stages, task cohorts, correctness, side-effect safety, cold installation, interaction wait, or external latency
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because one wall-clock number can punish deliberate confirmation, hide setup or external delay, and reward a fast but unsafe or incorrect command
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: manual wait is counted as tool latency without label, cached and cold runs mix, only successful runs remain, response time ends before effect verification, or tool-call reduction is assumed beneficial
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: evaluate command workflow performance and separate called script, MCP server, or production service throughput into dedicated tests
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define staged measurement, matched cohorts, correctness and effect gates, cold-versus-warm runs, failure inclusion, low-sample alternatives, and transparent uncertainty
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the meaningful unit is a verified workflow outcome; command speed that increases approval noise, context, or recovery cost is negative optimization
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to measure cold discovery, warm invocation, user-decision wait, tool and script execution, model processing, recovery, and total verified completion separately on matched task classes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because one wall-clock number can punish deliberate confirmation, hide setup or external delay, and reward a fast but unsafe or incorrect command
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; manual wait is counted as tool latency without label, cached and cold runs mix, only successful runs remain, response time ends before effect verification, or tool-call reduction is assumed beneficial
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: evaluate command workflow performance and separate called script, MCP server, or production service throughput into dedicated tests
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: define staged measurement, matched cohorts, correctness and effect gates, cold-versus-warm runs, failure inclusion, low-sample alternatives, and transparent uncertainty
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the meaningful unit is a verified workflow outcome; command speed that increases approval noise, context, or recovery cost is negative optimization

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded discovery, production traffic, parallel edits, context drift, and large codebases, but command scale also fails through namespace growth, shared state, integration fanout, and compatibility matrices
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because as commands multiply, duplicated prompt logic, broad permissions, collisions, inconsistent arguments, shared state, and platform combinations create system behavior that no single Markdown review can cover
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an umbrella command dispatches unrelated systems, several commands write the same state, distributed agents edit one artifact, integration combinations grow unbounded, or marketplace claims exceed tested installations
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this statement for plugin command architecture and ownership, not production-service capacity without explicit operational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add namespace and portfolio boundaries, state and effect ownership, shared-library rules, integration isolation, compatibility matrices, release coordination, and decommission gates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale is primarily contract coordination: once two commands can mutate the same state or promise inconsistent semantics, adding more prompt detail cannot restore local reasoning
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to split by user outcome and ownership, namespace discoverable command families, keep state local and versioned, isolate external integrations, centralize shared deterministic libraries, and require coordinated release and compatibility evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because as commands multiply, duplicated prompt logic, broad permissions, collisions, inconsistent arguments, shared state, and platform combinations create system behavior that no single Markdown review can cover
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; an umbrella command dispatches unrelated systems, several commands write the same state, distributed agents edit one artifact, integration combinations grow unbounded, or marketplace claims exceed tested installations
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this statement for plugin command architecture and ownership, not production-service capacity without explicit operational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add namespace and portfolio boundaries, state and effect ownership, shared-library rules, integration isolation, compatibility matrices, release coordination, and decommission gates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies scale is primarily contract coordination: once two commands can mutate the same state or promise inconsistent semantics, adding more prompt detail cannot restore local reasoning
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: each command has one owner and contract, shared components have tested interfaces, namespaces remain understandable, state and effects do not overlap silently, and release fixtures cover supported environments
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because as commands multiply, duplicated prompt logic, broad permissions, collisions, inconsistent arguments, shared state, and platform combinations create system behavior that no single Markdown review can cover
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where an umbrella command dispatches unrelated systems, several commands write the same state, distributed agents edit one artifact, integration combinations grow unbounded, or marketplace claims exceed tested installations
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by use this statement for plugin command architecture and ownership, not production-service capacity without explicit operational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in each command has one owner and contract, shared components have tested interfaces, namespaces remain understandable, state and effects do not overlap silently, and release fixtures cover supported environments
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that scale is primarily contract coordination: once two commands can mutate the same state or promise inconsistent semantics, adding more prompt detail cannot restore local reasoning
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: an umbrella command dispatches unrelated systems, several commands write the same state, distributed agents edit one artifact, integration combinations grow unbounded, or marketplace claims exceed tested installations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are name collisions across plugins, duplicated descriptions, inconsistent option semantics, cascading updates, old state schemas, cross-command recursive invocation, and support burden hidden by successful author tests
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where each command has one owner and contract, shared components have tested interfaces, namespaces remain understandable, state and effects do not overlap silently, and release fixtures cover supported environments
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using use this statement for plugin command architecture and ownership, not production-service capacity without explicit operational design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: split plugins by domain, expose a script or service API, use hooks for shared enforcement, federate MCP integrations, generate common documentation from one source, or narrow supported platforms and versions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the corpus supplies no maximum command count, integration count, or marketplace scale benchmark
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: split plugins by domain, expose a script or service API, use hooks for shared enforcement, federate MCP integrations, generate common documentation from one source, or narrow supported platforms and versions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine when one command, one plugin command set, or one owner can no longer provide a coherent, safely testable interface

## Section 025: Future Refresh Search Queries
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed supplies generic official-docs, GitHub-example, and release-note queries but does not define drift triggers, version and feature qualifiers, authoritative-source ranking, or reconciliation with installed command behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because search locates candidate evidence rather than validating syntax or semantics; source acceptance and fixture reproduction prevent snippets, mirrors, or latest-version docs from silently changing a pinned contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: result snippets become facts, current docs are assumed backward compatible, community examples define permissions, absence of results proves removal, or routine browsing is called verification

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: labels decorate unsourced paragraphs, archived examples become current facts, one successful invocation proves portability, MCP evidence proves native metadata, or uncertainty is detached from the release decision
